1934.12.05

Representative Luo Submits Memorandum Requesting Reduction of Annuity 1

China's Economy Faces Difficulties, Annuity Burden Too Heavy

Northeast Lost, Income Decreased, Making it Increasingly Difficult to Cope

Finance Committee to Discuss the Case 2

(Geneva) Luo Zhongyi, Chinese Minister to Denmark, after attending the UN General Assembly, remained in Geneva to address the issue of the Chinese government's payment of annuities to the League of Nations. Today, Mr. Luo submitted a memorandum to the Secretary regarding the annuity issue, making statements and suggestions. The full text is roughly divided into six sections. The first section is an introduction, stating that the purpose of this memorandum is to extend the declaration made by the Chinese delegation to the Fourth Committee of the 15th Assembly, and substantiate it with various figures and data. Other detailed points will be telegraphed to me by the Chinese government this month and will be successively submitted to the Secretariat as attachments. The second section is a historical background, stating that during the period of the former Beijing government, the proportion of annuities paid by China was too high, and payments were often not made on time. After the establishment of the National Government, it agreed in 1930 to divide the arrears into ten installments, paying an annual amount of 480,000 Swiss francs. However, it also requested that future annuity payments be reduced by half. Only the General Assembly has the authority to approve increases or decreases in member states' annuities. However, the Chinese government's intention is that if the annuity can be reduced by half after the arrears are cleared, it would be appropriate before the exact amount of the annuity is determined. Chinese representatives have repeatedly raised this matter in 1931 and 1932, but the League of Nations insisted that it should only be discussed from 1934 onwards. The third section states that the annuity borne by the Chinese government is indeed too heavy. This is the most important reason for requesting a reduction. The annuity amount was determined at a time of economic prosperity, flourishing trade, and high prices. The value of Chinese currency was also much higher than it is now. The situation is now different. If China has to continue to bear this amount, it will reach 3% of the total national expenditure. Compared with European countries where this burden only accounts for 0.01% or 0.03% of the total national expenditure, the difference is incalculable. The fourth section states that since the loss of the four northeastern provinces, China's income has greatly decreased. Direct tax revenues from postal services, telecommunications, railways, aviation, and international trade have all been severely affected, making it even more difficult. The fifth section describes the major disasters suffered by China in the past four years, which have had a profound and growing impact on the people's livelihood and national income. Other member states are often granted special permission to reduce annuities when they encounter disasters. China can also cite this precedent and request a reduction. The sixth section argues that some believe that if China reduces its annuity, international technical cooperation will be affected. However, the League of Nations budget was being discussed when China's request for a reduction in the annuity was being negotiated. Other countries, such as Greece, also receive benefits from League of Nations technical cooperation through special donations. Currently, China is affected by the global economic downturn and suffers from both natural and man-made disasters. The financial situation is extremely difficult and there is no sign of recovery. The standard of living is low, and even a very small amount is urgently needed. Representative Luo's memorandum will be discussed at the Finance Committee meeting on the 12th of this month. (Central News Agency dispatch, 3rd)

Mr. Branko Praises Our Country's Anti-Drug Program 3

丨Radio Speech Last Night丨

Hopes to Eradicate Opium to Revive the Nation

(Geneva) Mr. Branko, Director of the Narcotics Intelligence Bureau, gave a radio speech tonight, clarifying the work of the Opium Advisory Committee. He stated that one of the most important cases in this meeting is the new anti-drug program of the Chinese government. Mr. Branko said that the Chinese government faces many difficulties in effectively eradicating drugs, but the new program and regulations are comprehensive. If they can be implemented effectively, opium and other drugs can be eradicated within six years. Mr. Branko also said that the losses suffered by China due to the people's opium consumption are almost incalculable, and the illegal profits obtained by drug traffickers are also extremely alarming. During these six years, if the Chinese government implements a monopoly plan, the income will be substantial, but it will become a kind of temptation to continue the monopoly after the deadline. Mr. Branko expressed his respect for Chairman Chiang's determination to ban opium, saying that Chiang bears extremely heavy responsibilities, and hopes that his plan will succeed in eradicating opium and other narcotics within six years, so that the Chinese people can be saved from the scourge of drugs, the nation can become stronger, and the future of unification can be relied upon. Criticism of China's new plan is not yet timely, and it is necessary to wait for a year to observe its effectiveness before making a decision. (Central News Agency dispatch, 3rd)

Current Affairs Commentary

What is Expected of the Academic Work Advisory Center 季 24

The Academic Work Advisory Center is jointly established by the National Economic Council and the Ministry of Education. Since its establishment, it has sought to connect with vocational introduction agencies in various regions to enhance the effectiveness of assisting unemployed youth. The Advisory Center has formulated liaison measures, including the [Survey Form for Graduates of Colleges and Above] and the [Work Advisory Registration Certificate], which have been sent to the graduate affairs departments of various universities for review and implementation as a preliminary form of connection. Today, young people who have received higher education are struggling to find employment. The intention behind this initiative is undoubtedly beyond reproach. However, there are still things we feel compelled to express, and we would like to present them.

Today, the competition for jobs in our society is becoming increasingly fierce. Any vacancies in relatively prestigious positions are quickly seized by those who are skilled at maneuvering. The infighting and conflicts that arise from the struggle for positions are commonplace and no longer surprising. Even if the Advisory Center has good intentions for introductions, it may find there is little demand. Observe the public and private institutions everywhere; each time they recruit personnel, they invariably rely on referrals from relatives and friends, and recommendations are often made by powerful individuals. Those who rely on public introduction agencies can be said to be few and far between, and if there are any, they are likely positions that ordinary people despise and are unwilling to take. The government established the examination system for the purpose of selecting talented individuals. However, in the past two national higher examinations, only one or two hundred people were admitted. Even with the government's position, arranging positions for them is still deeply challenging, let alone for others. It is said that among these one or two hundred people, less than half can obtain official positions, and many still rely on personal connections. It can be seen that finding a job is difficult, and helping others to succeed is equally challenging.

Now that the Academic Work Advisory Center seeks to connect with vocational introduction agencies in various regions, we cannot but acknowledge its ambition to [gather wisdom and broaden ideas] and [facilitate cooperation and simplify tasks]. However, to say that this initiative alone can increase employment opportunities and directly benefit relief efforts is probably not necessarily true. However, the responsibility in this regard does not lie with the Advisory Center. The deep-rooted departmentalism in various places, the decline of production industries, and the inadequacy of past educational policies are all factors contributing to the unemployment phenomenon. To seek fundamental remedies, it is necessary to awaken those in power nationwide who have the right to employ people, and to improve education, production, and other industries. However, this matter is of great importance and cannot be achieved overnight. During this transitional period, we can only seek secondary solutions. Therefore, we dare to make two requests: (1) The Advisory Center is organized by the National Economic Council and the Ministry of Education, and its purpose is to assist in relieving youth unemployment through introduction. Why not first request its governing bodies (i.e., the Economic Council and the Ministry of Education) to directly place talented unemployed youth, to the best of their ability, as an example for other institutions? (2) The Advisory Center should increase personnel and expand activities. In addition to communicating with various vocational introduction agencies, it should also maintain close contact with important institutions within and outside Beijing that have direct hiring authority, in preparation for future introductions when vacancies arise. The effectiveness of this may be limited, but we hope that those in power in various institutions will gradually learn to identify and promote true talent and not be surrounded by relatives, friends, and powerful individuals. At that time, instead of each institution searching for candidates on its own and feeling disappointed or discouraged, it would be better to have a government agency representative to screen them.

Min Bandit Areas Fully Recovered After Capturing Ninghua 25

◎Longyan: The Eastern Route Army captured Ninghua, uncovered the pseudo-Jiangxi Soviet organs hiding in the area, and captured many key bandit personnel. Only Ninghua County remained in the Min bandit area, and now it has been captured. The bandit areas of Fujian Province have been completely recovered. (Central News Agency dispatch, 4th)

(Fuzhou) The 52nd Division captured Ninghua County on the 1st and advanced on the 3rd. Hundreds of remnants of the Sha bandits' pseudo 7th Army Corps' Young and Strong Brigade resisted stubbornly in dangerous terrain. They were defeated on the 2nd. Currently, only the Chenkeng-Hutou area of the county still has scattered bandits. Lu Shi has dispatched teams to search and eliminate them within a set time. The Executive Yuan appointed Liu Yigong as the Special Commissioner for Bandit Suppression Supervision on the Border of Fujian, Zhejiang, and Jiangxi. Wei Lihuang telegraphed that the bandit gang of Liang Yubao, who were harassing the Song-Zheng border, had been defeated by teams dispatched by Liu Heding's army. There is no trace of bandits near Zhengdun on the Song-Zheng border. (Special dispatch, 4th)

(London) The failure of the Chinese Jiangxi Communist Party has attracted considerable attention from various countries. The Manchester Guardian believes that the resistance of the Chinese Communist Party is gradually decreasing and expresses satisfaction. It states that since the Communist Party has failed, the Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, Chiang Kai-shek, will propose various measures to seek national unification at the Fifth Plenary Session of the Kuomintang, without the need to resolve internal affairs by force. Furthermore, the last base of the Red bandits in Fujian Province, Qingliu County, was captured by the National Army on November 27th. At the same time, the Red bandits are retreating steadily, and the National Army is reporting frequent victories. Chairman Chiang has ordered the complete clearing of the front lines and the disbanding of the Southwest and Northwest Bandit Suppression Headquarters. Although this news should be treated with caution as usual, it is believable that the resistance of the Red bandits has been destroyed. The newspaper continues that the Communist Party has occupied Jiangxi for several years and has been the greatest obstacle to China's peace and unification. Now that the National Army has directly attacked the bandit nest, the so-called "Red Country" has been eliminated, which is deeply gratifying. The Chinese authorities have continuously issued declarations on peaceful unification, and it is hoped that this time, it will produce good results. (Havas dispatch, 3rd)

Regulations on the Powers and Duties of the Commanders of the Pacification Zones in Fujian and Jiangxi 26

(Nanchang) After the establishment of the Pacification Headquarters in Jiangxi and Fujian, Jiangxi was divided into eight pacification zones, and Fujian was divided into four pacification zones. The Executive Yuan recently stipulated the powers and duties of the commanders of each pacification zone. In addition to the designated National Army being under their command, all security teams, administrative supervisors, county magistrates, and political directors of special districts within their jurisdiction are under their dispatch and command. (Central News Agency dispatch, 4th)

(Nanchang) The intermediate-level military officer training class run by the Jiangxi Security Team will end in the middle of the month and will be assigned to various counties to form security regiments. Once the regiments are established, one-third of the original security teams in each county throughout the province will be drawn for the first term of conscription this year. The conscription numbers for the first, second, and third terms have also been stipulated. (Central News Agency dispatch, 4th) (Fuzhou) Chiang Ting-wen returned to Longyan at noon on the 3rd and went to Zhangzhou to organize the Pacification Headquarters. The location of the four pacification zone commanders will be determined within days. (Central News Agency dispatch, 4th)

(Fuzhou) The post-disaster reconstruction in Changting County is well underway. Postal and telecommunications services will be restored within the month. (Central News Agency dispatch, 4th)

Bandit Rebels in Guangxi Have Been Defeated 27

(Hong Kong) Provincial news: Bai Chongxi telegraphed Guangdong on the evening of the 3rd, reporting a victory, stating that the bandit rebels who invaded Guangxi have now been completely defeated. In a series of fierce battles over five days, more than 1,000 bandits were killed, over 2,000 guns were seized, and over 2,000 prisoners were captured. Among them, more than 500 Guangxi bandits originally belonged to Li Mingrui's troops and have been sent to the province for reform. The rest are mostly from Hunan and Jiangxi and are now being sent to the central government for disposal. (Central News Agency dispatch, 4th)

Hunan, Hubei, Sichuan, and Guizhou Armies Jointly Encircle and Suppress the He Bandits 28

(Hankou) The Hunan, Hubei, Sichuan, and Guizhou armies are jointly advancing to suppress the He bandits and have already surrounded them. Someone has been appointed as the commander of the reserve army column. The units of someone, someone, someone, someone, someone, and someone are all under their command for suppression. (Special dispatch, 4th)

Order Restored on Zhejiang Border 29

Fang Zhimin's Remnants Flee to Anhui

(Hangzhou) The remnants of the Red bandit Fang Zhimin, who recently fled into Zhejiang, have, after the military authorities quickly dispatched a large army to encircle and suppress them, fled into Anhui Province as of the 4th. Local order has been completely restored. Yu Jishi returned to the province at 5:00 PM today. According to him, the bandits passing through Zhejiang were all in remote villages and towns and did not dare to attack county seats. The bandits in Wanshoufang have already been routed. On the evening of the 3rd, more than 3,000 bandits engaged our army in a fierce battle overnight in Baiguozhuang, Changhua County. The bandits suffered hundreds of casualties and were defeated by our army this morning. By this afternoon, they had completely fled to Jixi, Anhui Province. There are no longer any bandits in Zhejiang. (Special dispatch, 4th)

Severe Credit Crunch in Jinan 30

(Jinan) Recently, due to unscrupulous merchants smuggling silver dollars to Dalian, banks in the city are preparing cash to prevent bank runs. Currently, 3 to 4 million yuan in cash has been transferred from Shanghai, and withdrawals are being made from various silver firms, leading to a severe credit crunch. Shanghai drafts are down 18 yuan per thousand, and Shanghai remittances are down 13 yuan. Interest rates for two-month loans have risen to 1.75%. Because banks are not lending, there is little cash in the market. Transactions of major commodities such as cotton, cotton yarn, raw rice, and food have sharply decreased. (Special dispatch, 4th)

Transaction Tax Expected to be Levied Next Spring 31

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance's draft for levying transaction taxes is still under review by the commercial law and finance groups of the Legislative Yuan. It is understood that this tax is different from the exchange tax. The exchange tax is a purely profitable nature and has been levied for some time. The transaction tax is levied on both buyers and sellers in the market, similar to a business tax. For example, once a transaction is completed, both parties should bear the statutory tax amount equally, just like the commission paid by both parties to the broker. However, for the broker, it becomes a customary handling fee, while this is a legitimate state tax, specifically levied on both parties, with similar circumstances. As for the tax rate standards, public bonds will be based on a unit of 10,000 yuan, bullion will be based on each tael, and other items such as goods, securities, cotton yarn, flour, miscellaneous grains, and oils will be calculated by package, carload (for grains), or catty (for oils). For example, public bonds will be taxed at approximately 1.5 yuan per 10,000 yuan, bullion will be taxed at approximately 0.1 yuan per tael, and cotton yarn will be taxed at approximately 3 yuan per package. After the tax is levied, it is expected to generate 3 to 4 million yuan in tax revenue annually. The collection procedures will be handled by the respective exchanges. However, because it still needs to be passed by the Legislative Yuan and undergo promulgation procedures, it is expected that it can only be levied in the spring of next year. (Special dispatch, 4th)

Ministry of Finance Promulgates Rules for Inspecting Stamps 32

(Nanjing) After the Ministry of Finance issued the pagoda-style new stamps, it changed the inspection matters and asked the provincial, municipal, and county governments to preside over them. The Ministry recently promulgated fifteen rules for inspecting stamps to be followed by the inspection personnel. (Central News Agency dispatch, 4th)

Page 6

Kato Questions the Manchuria Issue at the Japanese Budget Committee

Okada, Hirota, and Hayashi Respond Separately

Extraordinary Diet Session Decides to Extend for Three Days

(Tokyo) The House of Representatives Budget Committee convened at 10:00 AM today to continue questioning. The first questioner today was Kato Kumejiro. Kato raised questions regarding policies towards Manchuria and the issue of agencies in Manchuria. He emphasized the contradiction of the Commander of the Kwantung Army concurrently serving as the Plenipotentiary Ambassador, and the necessity of revising and strengthening the Japan-Manchukuo Protocol, attracting everyone's attention. The content of Kato's discussion with the various ministers is as follows:

Kato asked: When the government implemented reforms to the administrative organs stationed in Manchuria, were there instances of disrupting official discipline? Does the government intend to punish those responsible?

Prime Minister Okada replied: It is regrettable that different opinions were raised from various sides before the decision to reform the agencies stationed in Manchuria.

Kato asked: How is the bandit suppression in Manchuria progressing?

Minister of the Army Hayashi replied: There are currently small bandit groups scattered throughout Manchuria, numbering approximately 30,000 to 40,000. The Japanese army is continuing to suppress them.

Kato asked: What is the command system between the Ambassador stationed in Manchuria and the Commander of the Kwantung Army?

Foreign Minister Hirota replied: They are currently on an equal footing.

Kato asked: Is this reform of the agencies stationed in Manchuria a temporary reform?

Prime Minister Okada replied: In the future, as the security of [Manchukuo] is improved, the organization will change again. Therefore, in this sense, it can be considered a temporary reform. Kato asked: Is the Ambassador stationed in Manchuria and the Commander of the Kwantung Army not held by the same person concurrently?

Prime Minister Okada replied: They are the same person.

Kato asked: Then, is the candidate for Plenipotentiary Ambassador limited to the Army Commander?

Prime Minister Okada replied: Yes.

Kato asked: When the Army appoints the Commander of the Kwantung Army, does it consult with the Prime Minister on the candidate?

Minister of the Army Hayashi replied: Appointing an Army Commander falls under the Supreme Command and does not require consultation with the Prime Minister. However, when appointing a Plenipotentiary Ambassador, consultation is necessary. Kato then pointed out the contradiction of the Kwantung Army Commander, who is appointed after being reported to the Emperor, and the Plenipotentiary Ambassador, who is appointed after a Cabinet decision, being held by the same person. He pressed the Prime Minister to the end, but the Prime Minister's responses lacked clarity.

Kato further asked: If the official system is established, and the Army Commander is under the supervision of the Prime Minister, can the Prime Minister completely supervise him?

Prime Minister Okada replied: He can supervise him.

Kato asked about the issue of Supreme Command and the issue of supervision, pressing the Prime Minister. Prime Minister Okada also debated with him. Kato then mentioned the Japan-Manchukuo Protocol.

Kato asked: Since Japan intends to develop [Manchukuo], should the Japan-Manchukuo Protocol be concluded with more detailed treaties to promote Japan-Manchukuo amity? Although [Manchukuo] is an independent country, it has close relations with Japan. Without Japan's active assistance, its development cannot be expected. What do the Army Minister and Foreign Minister believe?

Minister of the Army Hayashi replied: He shares the same opinion as Mr. Kato.

Foreign Minister Hirota replied: Upholding the independence of [Manchukuo] is not only Japan's great ideal but also the foundation of peace in East Asia. Therefore, Japan does not hesitate to provide active assistance.

Kato asked: How is the diplomatic work progressing?

Foreign Minister Hirota replied: There is no need to conclude new treaties in addition to the Japan-Manchukuo Protocol.

Kato asked: Does the Foreign Minister have the intention to be responsible for strengthening the Japan-Manchukuo Protocol?

Foreign Minister Hirota replied: Japan and Manchukuo have a special relationship, and I intend to work hard to fulfill my duties.

When it was noon, Kato temporarily stopped questioning, and the meeting recessed.

The Budget Committee continued its meeting in the afternoon. Mr. Kato pursued the Army Minister regarding the issue of agencies stationed in Manchuria and the procedures for appointing the Commander of the Kwantung Army. Thereupon, Army Minister Hayashi rose and answered as follows: When deciding on the Army Commander, the three senior officials of the Army will deliberate before making a decision. Everything is considered appropriate. As for the Army Commander as Plenipotentiary Ambassador, he should consult with the Prime Minister. If he fails to obtain the Prime Minister's consent, the three senior officials must reconsider and strive to align their views with the Prime Minister's before proceeding.

Kato asked: The Army Minister's remarks seem to narrow the scope and boundaries of reporting to the Emperor. I have this understanding. However, the issue of the League of Nations' agencies stationed in Manchuria, which arose from ending the police officers of the Kwantung Government-General, is this related to the responsibility of the Minister of Colonial Affairs?

As Kato finished speaking, he directed his gaze directly at the Prime Minister. Thereupon, Prime Minister Okada rose and replied: When reforming the agencies stationed in Manchuria, the general public's so-called state of opposition within the government departments is definitely not the case. There may have been misunderstandings, but today, those misunderstandings have long been dispelled.

Kato asked: To maintain the security of Manchuria, is it necessary for the commander of the military police to concurrently serve as the chief of police of the Kwantung Government-General? What is the reason? Army Minister Hayashi explained the details as follows: There are two reasons: The situation in Manchuria has changed since the independence of [Manchukuo]. Therefore, the unification of the police is necessary for the security of Manchuria. Hence, it is placed under the jurisdiction of the military police. This is one of the reasons. The center of Manchurian administration is in the Kwantung Government-General. Therefore, external conspiracies all arise from the Kwantung Government-General and the South Manchuria Railway-affiliated areas. Moreover, since [Manchukuo] is not yet consolidated, the police in the heart of Manchuria, i.e., the Kwantung Leased Territory, must also be placed under the jurisdiction of the commander of the military police. This may cause some grievances to the police officers of the Government-General, but it is truly unavoidable due to the circumstances. It is definitely not the military monopolizing police power. The supplementary appointment of the Army Commander is indeed an exercise of the Supreme Command.

Kato asked: What is the Army Minister's view on the joint defense in the Japan-Manchukuo Protocol?

Minister of the Army Hayashi replied: Maintaining the security of Manchuria is not only for suppressing bandits. In terms of relations with neighboring countries, it is for stabilizing internal morale and establishing the foundation of [Manchukuo]. Combining these various circumstances is what is called national defense.

Kato asked: I heard that an economic conference between Japan and Manchukuo is to be established. What does the Prime Minister believe?

Prime Minister Okada replied: It is still undecided in the current Cabinet.

Kato asked: How will the Japan-Manchukuo tariff issue be resolved?

Foreign Minister Hirota rose and replied: We are currently working on it and will realize it.

Kato asked: Regarding the organization of the new economy of Manchuria, there are various rumors in the world. The so-called state socialism is quite contrary to our national conditions. What is the Army's view?

Minister of the Army Hayashi replied: I am not aware of this matter. However, if the agencies stationed in Manchuria are established, there will not be such extreme situations. It may even be possible to discover an ideal economic organization.

Kato asked: Recently, there have been general discussions about unconditionally returning the South Manchuria Railway-affiliated areas within [Manchukuo]. What is the truth?

Prime Minister Okada replied: We cannot unconditionally return them. It is always necessary to consider it carefully.

Mr. Kato's questioning concluded here. Next, Mr. Shimizu will raise questions.

Mr. Shimizu Ginzo made a general inquiry on how to operate constitutional government at the Budget Committee. Next, after questioning Finance Minister Takahashi regarding the issue of responsibility, he raised the issue of diplomacy towards China, questioning its direction. Foreign Minister Hirota replied:

Maintaining peace in the Orient is the fundamental spirit.

Shimizu asked:

Is diplomacy towards China following the consistent direction as stated by the Foreign Minister?

Foreign Minister Hirota replied:

If it is the policy of the Japanese Empire, there is only one line; there is no reason for two.

Mr. Shimizu's questioning concluded here. Next, Saito Takao of the Constitutional Democratic Party asked questions centered on disaster countermeasures. Then, the meeting was temporarily recessed at 5:40 PM and reopened at 7:00 PM. It is said that it will be adjourned only late at night.

The term of the 66th Extraordinary Diet session was originally scheduled to expire on the 4th. The government, in light of the discussion of the budget proposal, convened an extraordinary Cabinet meeting in the Diet at 4:45 PM on the 4th. As a result of the deliberation, it was decided to extend the session for three days. It was immediately approved by the Emperor, and the edict was published in the official gazette extraordinary edition on the same day. (Domei dispatch, 4th)

Britain and America Cooperate in Dealing with the Far East Situation 33

Hull Expresses Enthusiastic Approval

Reiterates Unchanged Traditional Policy

Maintaining Peace and Open Door

(Washington) British-American cooperation has become even stronger today after Secretary of State Hull issued a frank and cautious statement. Mr. Hull stated to the press that he supports the British-American cooperation currently underway in London. Although the wording of the statement broadly refers to closer economic cooperation among countries around the world, its intention clearly refers to Britain. However, Mr. Hull carefully avoided expressing that British-American cooperation is opposed to Japan's naval demands or the [Manchukuo] oil monopoly incident. Mr. Hull believes that the naval issue should be discussed by the three-nation representatives in London, and the oil issue should be handled separately by Britain and the United States. However, according to the State Department's recent review of American Far East policy, it has been decided to maintain the traditional policies of peace, the open door, and avoiding combinations that could cause disputes, regardless of what combinations other countries may have in the Far East. The British authorities have sought American views on what action to take after Japan abolishes the naval treaty. Diplomatic circles believe that Britain intends to establish British-American naval coordination, so that the United States will propose concrete conditions in exchange for British cooperation in maintaining the political and naval status quo in the Far East. Mr. Hull's remarks today indicate that the State Department supports economic ties but is unwilling to go beyond the scope of economic ties. (Kokumin dispatch, 3rd)

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull issued a statement today criticizing the remarks made by American Ambassador to Britain, Bingham, published in the London Observer on December 2nd, saying that in the past few years, world economic events have been undermined by the extreme isolationism and nationalism. Bingham's remarks can be said to be an effort to eliminate this spirit. The United States is willing to seek sincere and practical cooperation with many countries to remove obstacles in international finance and commerce. Other countries can act jointly with the United States in their own independent ways. Washington officials generally believe that Hull's remarks support Bingham but do not focus solely on cooperation between Britain and the United States, fearing that it will cause misunderstandings among countries such as Japan. According to Ambassador Bingham's remarks, the main purpose is to promote British-American cooperation. His words include "If Britain and the United States firmly grasp the current opportunity and initiate close cooperation, the world's panic can be dispelled soon, and various diplomatic difficulties in the world can be solved easily. If Britain and President Roosevelt reach an understanding, it will be equivalent to establishing a permanent understanding with the American people," etc. (Reuters dispatch, 3rd)

US-Japan Meeting Still Yields No Results

Naval Negotiations Continue Despite the Odds

(London) The British and American naval delegations will meet this afternoon in the British House of Commons. This is the first time in several weeks. The Japanese side claims that the abolition of the treaty will not affect the current naval talks because it only involves the provisions of not establishing defensive works. Britain does not seem to accept this view. (Reuters dispatch, 4th)

(London) After the luncheon hosted by British delegation head Davis, representative Yamamoto met alone with Admiral Stanley, but they did not discuss substantive issues. Yamamoto left without gaining anything. It seems that Yamamoto and Stanley will not meet again in the future. The attitude of the American delegation remains unchanged. Whether there is hope for the future of the talks depends on the outcome of the British-Japanese talks. The Japanese government has decided to abolish the Washington Treaty, and the possibility of the American delegation returning home is becoming more and more certain. (Domei dispatch, 3rd) (London) At noon today, the American naval delegation hosted a banquet for the naval representatives of Britain and Japan. After the banquet, American officials believed that although the Japanese side still insisted on giving up the ratio system and demanding naval equality, it seemed possible to concede to the British reconciliation plan's proposal to mutually notify each other of naval plans. Thus, there is some hope for the future of the naval talks. According to the British proposal on November 8, which was put forward to reconcile the opinions of the United States and Japan, it contained two suggestions. The main point was to recognize in principle Japan's equal rights in security, but the participating countries of the Naval Treaty should agree with a [gentlemen's agreement] to mutually notify each other of shipbuilding procedures and modifications. The naval plan notification mentioned in this telegram refers to this. (Havas dispatch, 3rd)

Opposing the Proposal of Regional Confrontation

(Washington dispatch, 4th)

◎ Rome The Japanese government recently requested that Italy and France jointly announce the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty. The Italian government rejected this request today. It is reported that the wording of the rejection stated that the Italian government is willing to strive to avoid any proposal that would create regional confrontation among countries. (Reuters dispatch, 3rd)

(Paris) Regarding Japan's request for France and Italy to simultaneously declare the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty, the information published in foreign newspapers is mostly incomplete. In reality, the French government replied to the Japanese government that the qualitative limitations stipulated in the Washington Naval Treaty no longer correspond with the French government's views. This is because when these qualitative limitations were established, the German navy had not yet recovered. Now, the situation has already changed. The French government is willing to jointly announce the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty with all signatory countries, but to avoid misunderstandings, France is delaying making a definitive decision on the Japanese government's special requests made during the London Naval Conference, and will not take joint action with the Japanese government. (Havas dispatch, 3rd)

(London) The American delegation believes that the Japanese government's cabinet decision on the 3rd to abandon the Washington Treaty procedures is an unexpected situation. The Disarmament Main Conference will be held in June next year. 2) The form of the abolition talks will be changed to ordinary diplomatic negotiations, and the former proposal is the most powerful. Japanese Delegation Issues Statement 37

(London) Regarding the naval conference talks, the following impressions were obtained from sources close to the Japanese delegation today. The delegation's spokesperson recently told our reporter, "Although Japan does not reject the British compromise proposal in general, it has not found a basis for establishing a three-nation agreement. There are various rumors circulating that our country's attitude has changed. We are taking this opportunity to deny them. Nothing said or proposed by our delegation can be interpreted as a change in attitude. What we are asking for can be summed up in one word: equal rights. Moreover, after equal rights are recognized, technical issues must be discussed to clarify whether these equal rights should be metaphysical or physical. (Note: Metaphysical refers to changing the naval ratio of 5:5:3 to 5:5:5, while physical refers to changing it from 5:5:3 to 3:3:3.) Only through these technical issues can the duration of the implementation of equal rights be determined. Regarding the mutual notification of each country's shipbuilding plans, some parties have expressed considerable optimism, but the actual solution is not easy to determine." When our reporter asked whether Japan's abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty would change the negotiation situation, the spokesperson replied, "This was decided by Tokyo long ago and does not seem to have any impact on the current talks." When the reporter asked if the naval talks would end from now on, the spokesperson replied, "This is not something we can decide." (Havas dispatch, 4th)

Comparison of Military Expenditures of Various Countries 38

Japan's Increased Fourfold Since the Manchurian Incident

France Ranks First in Air Force Strength, Japan Fourth

(Washington) According to the results of an investigation by the Foreign Policy Association, the military expenditures of the world's major powers, except for Germany, are generally greater than before the war. This state of armament has become particularly rapid since Japan's occupation of Manchuria in 1931 and the Nazi Party's assumption of power in Germany. The naval, land, and air force budgets of the major countries are as follows: France increased by 256% compared to 1913, Italy increased by 26.35%, England increased by 48.8%, the United States increased by 190.9%, and Japan increased by 388%. Japan's military spending has doubled since the Manchurian Incident. The United States' military expenditure was $244,000,000 in 1913, and by 1930 it had increased to over $700,000,000. Germany, however, is restricted by the Treaty of Versailles and cannot do as it pleases. As for the air force, France ranks first, with 3,000 military aircraft of various types. Soviet Russia ranks second, with 2,800 to 3,000 aircraft. The United States ranks third, with 2,468 aircraft. Japan has 1,600 aircraft. Italy has 1,500 aircraft. England has the fewest, with only 1,400 aircraft. (Kokumin dispatch, 4th)

Japan Mints Nickel Coins to Prepare for War 39

Purchasing Large Quantities of Raw Materials from Brazil

◎ Rio de Janeiro The Brazilian International Trade Bureau held a meeting today and announced that Japan recently purchased 40,000 tons of nickel from the Livramento mine in Brazil, and has placed another order for 40,000 tons. The announcement of this figure is related to the revision of the nickel export tax, as the amount of nickel exported recently has been very large. It is said that nickel is an important raw material for wartime. Japan has recently been minting nickel coins, hoping to accumulate a large amount to prepare for contingencies. (Kokumin dispatch, 3rd)

Saar Problem and South Hungarian Dispute Under Discussion

(London) The current session of the League of Nations Council will open tomorrow and a special conference will be held to discuss various issues related to the Saar plebiscite. Although the meeting is convened for the Saar problem, it may also discuss Yugoslavia's complaint that Hungary was involved in the Marseille assassination. According to the Yugoslav government's memorandum to the League of Nations last week, evidence was presented proving that terrorist organizations were established within Hungary. However, the text lacks clarity regarding whether the Hungarian authorities were aware of and supported it. The British Lord Privy Seal, Anthony Eden, has already departed for Geneva today to participate in the special conference. Soviet Foreign Commissar Maxim Litvinov is also en route to Geneva from Moscow. (Reuters dispatch, 3rd)

(Geneva) French Foreign Minister Laval, accompanied by the director of the French delegation to the League of Nations, Massigli, and the director of political affairs of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Bargeton, departed from Paris to attend the extraordinary meeting of the Council of the League of Nations (to be held tomorrow to discuss the Saar problem), and arrived here at 8:30 this morning. British Lord Privy Seal Anthony Eden and Yugoslav Foreign Minister Jevtić arrived in the same train as Laval. (Havas dispatch, 4th)

(Geneva) French Foreign Minister Laval arrived here this morning and immediately held talks with French experts on the Saar problem, followed by a meeting with Aloisi, chairman of the Three-Member Committee on the Saar problem. Aloisi will present an explanation of the committee's discussions in Rome. At noon, Laval hosted a banquet for Czech Foreign Minister Beneš, Yugoslav Foreign Minister Jevtić, and Yugoslav Permanent Representative to the League of Nations, Živojin Balugdžić. After the banquet, the three foreign ministers jointly discussed various issues, including: 1) the Saar problem; 2) Yugoslavia's application to the League of Nations regarding the Marseille assassination; 3) the plan for an Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact. The League of Nations' Three-Member Committee on the Saar problem is scheduled to meet at 4:00 PM to complete its report, so that it can be submitted to the member states of the Council tomorrow morning. The Council will hold a closed-door meeting tomorrow afternoon to decide on the procedures to be adopted regarding Yugoslavia's application, and then hold a public meeting to study the report of the Three-Member Committee on the Saar problem. It is generally believed that in the closed-door meeting of the Council, the Yugoslav representative will first formally submit the application, followed by the Hungarian representative submitting a reply. Then, the representatives of the major powers will issue statements. Some countries, such as Britain and Italy, will likely advocate postponing the discussion. However, the majority of the member states of the Council, especially Yugoslavia, will not be satisfied with this procedure. If so, even if a motion is proposed to study a general convention to prevent terrorist acts to conclude the matter, it may not be sufficient. The Council will likely strive to extend the meeting in a spirit of compromise and pass a resolution condemning the Marseille assassination and acts of terrorism in strong terms, so that Yugoslavia may be comforted. (Havas dispatch, 4th)

Contents of Franco-German Agreement on Saar Financial Issues 43

Assuming the Vote Results in Return to Germany

Germany Should Repay French Debt of 900 Million Francs

The Warndt Mines Should Pay Royalties for Five Years

◎ Rome France and Germany reached an agreement here today regarding various issues in the Saar region. The details are as follows: The agreement states that if the Saar plebiscite on January 13 results in a vote in favor of the Saar remaining part of Germany, then France should receive 900 million francs and 11 million tons of coal. In addition, France should receive royalties for five years from the production of the Warndt mines, amounting to approximately 45 million francs. These two mine entrances are located in French territory, while the ore veins extend into Saar territory. The Warndt coal mine is mined by Germany, and the royalties are paid directly to the French Ministry of Finance. However, it is said that all the coal mined belongs to Germany. It is also stipulated that if Germany has not paid off the 900 million francs after five years, 600 million of it will be used to offset the costs of houses, railways, etc., built by the French authorities in the Saar region. It is heard that the paper money currently circulating in the Saar region will be used as part of the payment. It is also heard that Saar residents must declare the actual amount of foreign currency they hold abroad. The 11 million tons of coal paid is part of the cash payment and is the annual output of the Saar coal mine. Germany also promises to guarantee the safety of Saar residents who have not voted with social insurance, and must respect all the rights enjoyed by workers and freedom of religion. It is heard that both France and Germany are quite pleased with this agreement. (Reuters, 3rd)

German Special Envoy Returns to Berlin 44

(Paris) Joachim von Ribbentrop, the representative of the German leader and Chancellor Hitler, who met with Foreign Minister Laval, has now departed for home. When he left, reporters asked him about the impact of this conversation on the future of Europe. Ribbentrop smiled and replied, "Allow me to answer later." (Havas dispatch, 3rd)

Hidden Internal Worries in Germany 45

Goebbels' Called Adventurous Attempts

Said to be Related to the Government's Domestic Policy

(Berlin) The Nazi government has been experiencing various difficulties in politics, economics, and society. The Protestant Evangelical Church is also resisting the government over its religious policies. All of this is enough to diminish the prestige of the Nazi regime. Although Nazi Party members outwardly express calm, they are inwardly very anxious. According to observations by Evangelical Church members, the religious policy set by the government is based on the philosophy of racial supremacy and Nazism, in an attempt to unify the churches nationwide. There are fears that this is being done too hastily, which may cause dissatisfaction among Catholics and the Roman Catholic Church in the Saar region and adversely affect the Saar plebiscite. It has been decided to wait until after the plebiscite on January 13 next year before continuing. (Havas dispatch, 3rd)

(Berlin) The German Minister of Propaganda, Dr. Joseph Goebbels, made a statement today that Germany will have several tasks to do in the future, but the time is not yet ripe. Germany must make historically unprecedented positive and courageous attempts. A government that wants to make history must have the courage to decide on major plans. What he meant by these words has aroused inquiries from all sides. Goebbels told a Reuters reporter today that he had nothing more to say. What he said was related to the government's internal policy and was an expression of the workers' insurance plan. However, extreme Nazi Party members are speaking of foreign adventures regarding the subtle meaning of Goebbels' remarks. (Reuters dispatch, 3rd)

Belgium Borrows from the Netherlands 46

Totaling 100 Million Guilders

◎ Brussels The Belgian government has agreed to borrow from the Netherlands to meet the needs of the national treasury and implement an extraordinary budget. According to a report from the Belgian news agency, the total amount of this loan is 100 million guilders, of which 75 million guilders is the amount borrowed by Belgium at an interest rate of 4%. The remaining 25 million guilders will be used for the Belgian Congo in Africa. (Havas dispatch, 4th)

Turkish Women Gain the Right to Vote 47

◎ Ankara Turkish women aged 22 and over are expected to gain the right to vote soon, and those aged 32 and over will also be eligible to be elected as members of parliament. The ruling party proposed this suggestion today, and it is expected to become law soon. (Reuters dispatch, 4th)

Stalin and Hundreds of Thousands of Others Pay Their Last Respects to Kirov 48

Casket Moved to Moscow, Cremation Tonight

Leningrad Officials Dismissed

Seventy-One Arrested to be Tried by Military Court

(Moscow) Kirov's casket was moved to Moscow at 10:30 AM on Tuesday. The body will be temporarily placed in the Hall of Unions. The hall will be open from 4:00 PM on Tuesday to 10:00 PM on Wednesday, so that Moscow workers can go to pay their last respects. The burial is now scheduled for the night of the 5th. On the morning of the 6th, the urn containing the ashes will still be placed in the Hall of Unions. The public will be able to go to pay their respects again from 6:00 AM to 1:00 PM on the 6th. The funeral will be held on the 6th. Those carrying the urn will depart from the Hall of Unions at 2:30 PM on the 6th and proceed to Red Square, where a memorial service will be held on Lenin's Mausoleum. The Moscow Soviet has decided that the 3rd, 4th, and 6th of this month will be days of mourning. All entertainment, banquets, music, and performances will be suspended. (TASS dispatch, 4th)

◎ Leningrad Stalin, Voroshilov, Molotov, and Zhdanov have arrived in Leningrad since Kirov's death. People here have not slept all night. Kirov's casket is placed on a high platform in the Hall of Uritzky Palace. Hundreds of thousands of workers have been continuously going to pay their respects. The honor guard next to the coffin rotates every five minutes. A large number of wreaths sent by Stalin, Molotov, Voroshilov, and the Moscow Workers' Delegation surround the casket. The famous artist Manizer has made a face model for Kirov. The Uritzky Palace closed its doors at 3:00 AM and reopened at 5:00 AM, and visits to the coffin continued without interruption. Tonight, Kirov's body will stop being visited and will be sent to Moscow. Various factories here are electing delegations to go to Moscow to participate in the funeral. (TASS dispatch, 3rd)

◎ Leningrad Yesterday at 9:50 PM, Stalin, Molotov, Voroshilov, Zhdanov, and Chuduov were the last honor guard next to Kirov's casket. Afterward, they carried the casket out of the Uritzky iron gate and placed it on a gun carriage fully hung with battle flags. At 10:00 PM, the funeral procession set off for the train station, accompanied by hundreds of thousands of local workers. Red Army troops stood along both sides of the avenue from the Uritzky Palace to the train station. The procession arrived at the train station amidst torches and funeral music. At that time, Kirov's closest comrades, Leningrad Party members Chuduov, Ugarov, Kodatzky, Poseren, etc., carried the casket, flags, wreaths, etc., from the gun carriage. At midnight, the casket was carried into the center of the funeral train. The train was decorated with black and red cloth. The train was protected by a tank convoy. At 12:30 AM, the whistles of the various factories sounded together. At that time, all the locomotives in the station and the ships in the port sounded their whistles for five minutes as a final tribute. At that time, everything stopped. All traffic in the city was stopped, and the machinery in the factories also stopped working. Then, the train slowly left Leningrad. (TASS dispatch, 4th)

(Moscow) Today, Moscow has been looking forward to the arrival since dawn. Representatives of various factories, institutions, and organizations are marching to the train station with mourning flags in hand to meet the funeral train. When Kirov's casket arrived at the Moscow train station at 11:40 AM, the honor guard composed of members of the Political Bureau of the Central Committee, members of the Soviet government, old Bolsheviks, and Kirov's close comrades went to the platform to greet it. At that time, planes flew in formation in the sky. When the train arrived at the platform, mournful music played loudly. Stalin, Kaganovich, and other members of the Political Bureau carried the casket onto the gun carriage on the platform. The funeral procession carried a large number of wreaths, flags, and banners and proceeded from the train station to the Hall of Unions. Tens of thousands of Moscow workers stood on both sides of the street. Stalin, Molotov, Voroshilov, Kaganovich, Kalinin, and other members of the Political Bureau, the Central Committee, and the Soviet government closely followed the casket. The casket will be temporarily placed in the Hall of Unions, and a large number of Moscow workers will go to pay their respects. (TASS dispatch, 4th)

(Moscow) The Internal Affairs Commission issued a notice regarding the circumstances of Kirov's assassination. According to the investigation, Kirov was drafting a report on the plenary session of the Communist Party Central Committee in December, to be read at the meeting of the Leningrad Party Committee on the same day. When Kirov walked into his office in the Smolny Institute, the receptionist Nikolaev walked out of the neighboring room and approached Kirov from behind. He immediately fired his pistol at Kirov's neck. The assassin was arrested on the spot. Kirov lost consciousness immediately after suffering a fatal wound. He was immediately taken to the office for rescue. When Professors Dubotvorsky, Ganneles, Geser, etc., arrived, Kirov had no pulse and had stopped breathing. They injected adrenaline, ethyl ether, camphor, codeine, and used artificial respiration, but all were ineffective. The doctors then said that Kirov was dead. An autopsy was performed the next day, proving that the deceased was very strong. The cause of his death was a serious head injury caused by a bullet. At the same time, when Kirov fell, his left forehead hit the floor, so the left half of his brain was severely injured, the skull was severely fractured, and the brain was also violently shaken. (TASS dispatch, 4th)

(Moscow) A statement by the famous writer Maxim Gorky has been published. He said, "An outstanding figure, one of the most outstanding leaders of our party, an ideal example of the proletariat, an ambassador of culture, has now been assassinated. I sincerely express the same grief as our party and all loyal workers. Therefore, I must say one thing, that the success of the enemy this time not only shows the enemy's hatred, but also shows our lack of preparedness." (TASS dispatch, 4th)

(Moscow) The director of the Internal Affairs Commission's Leningrad office, Medvedev, the deputy director, Fomin, and the responsible personnel of the office, Golin, Lolev, Yerunishivsky, Petrov, Balrevich, and Mosevich, have been dismissed and investigated for neglecting their security duties. The Deputy Commissioner of the Internal Affairs Commission, Agranov, is temporarily concurrently serving as the director of the Leningrad office. Thirty-nine White Russians in the Leningrad region and thirty-two in the Moscow region, who were recently arrested for plotting and preparing to assassinate officials of the Soviet government, were transferred to the military court of the Supreme Court of the Soviet Union for trial on the 2nd of this month. (TASS) (Moscow) The Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union met on the 1st of this month and resolved: 1) To instruct the legal investigation agencies to accelerate the investigation of cases of those who have prepared or committed terrorist acts. 2) To instruct the courts not to allow death row inmates who participated in the aforementioned organizations to request amnesty or suspend execution, because the Central Executive Committee believes that such requests can never be accepted. 3) To instruct the agencies of the Internal Affairs Commission to execute prisoners belonging to the aforementioned organizations immediately after they have been convicted. (TASS, 3rd)

The Scope of the French Economic Conference is Broad 49

Planning Economic Liaison Between the Mainland and Colonies

(Paris) The French Colonial Conference opened here today to discuss economic reciprocity plans among the 4,680,000 square miles of French territories. The scope of the discussion is limited to industry, commerce, economics, budgets, tariffs, and other issues, so as to avoid purely unimportant local issues that would delay the process and lead to nowhere. Most of the work of this conference will discuss the issues of the territories of Algeria, Tunisia, Morocco, and Syria. However, other smaller territories, leased territories, and protectorates will not be neglected. Even the pearl and coconut industries in the French islands in the South China Sea, the rice industry in Vietnam, and the peanut and vegetable oil industries in Senegal will be discussed. The conference represents the interests of 100 million people. According to the Colonial Department, if the various colonies can abandon competition with each other and follow a large-scale liaison plan, commerce will definitely double. To achieve this goal, the various colonies may have to limit production for a certain period of time. Last year, the trade surplus of the colonies to the French mainland was the first time in history. One-third of France's foreign trade is with its territories. Before the global economic decline, colonial purchases of French goods increased annually. Now, if we want to restore commerce, the tariff issue is very important. The world's countries that trade with France and its twenty territories must also pay close attention. (Kokumin dispatch, 3rd)

American Blind Aviator Creates New High-Altitude Flight Record 50

14,600 Meters Above Ground

(New York) The American blind aviator, Russell Boardman, who was famous for his solo around-the-world flight, flew an airplane and ascended in Bartlesville, Oklahoma, this morning to attempt to break the world altitude record. He landed in Muskogee in the afternoon. According to him, the altitude reached was 14,630 meters. If so, the record of 14,433 meters created by the Italian aviator Donati has been broken by Boardman. (Havas, 3rd)

Australian Aviator's Long-Distance Flight Between America and Australia 51

Testing the Pacific Air Route

◎ Auckland Another plane departed from the Golden Gate today to test the Pacific air route. Australian long-distance aviator Charles Ulm, accompanied by John Little Jr., flew from the Auckland airfield to Honolulu at 2:43 PM. This is the first leg of the American-Australian flight. The plane was piloted by Ulm and took off very successfully. It soon flew away from above the Golden Gate. The plane is loaded with 825 gallons of oil. According to Ulm, the purpose of this trip is to test the civilian air route from the United States to Australia. It was originally planned to take off from Vancouver, but the weather in the Northwest was bad, so it was abandoned. The two plan to fly to Australia along the route of Kingsford Smith's ship. (Kokumin dispatch, 3rd)

Five people are missing and are said to have drowned. Twenty-five people in the Philippines have died in the storm this week. Reports and Statistics on Locust Control in Various Counties 62

Tan Zhen Discusses the Recovery of Consular Jurisdiction 63

(Nanjing) Tan Zhen stated that China had previously raised the issue of recovering consular jurisdiction, and several countries in the League of Nations had recognized it, while others advocated sending personnel to China for investigation to assess the extent to which China's judiciary had improved before making a decision. At that time, the League of Nations organized an investigation team to China in 1926, during the period when Zhang Zongchang and others were ravaging the judiciary in North China. The impression gained from the investigation was extremely poor, and various countries used this as an excuse to delay. Subsequently, after the government's vigorous negotiations, some progress was made, namely the abolition of the Shanghai Mixed Court and the conclusion of the agreement on the Shanghai Special District Court. Before long, national crises occurred, and China requested the League of Nations to resolve these more important matters than the judicial issue, so it was put aside. It is found that the said agreement had a validity period of three years, and after it expired last year, it was extended for another three years. At present, China's judicial improvements have made considerable progress, and various legal regulations to perfect the judiciary have also been promulgated and implemented one after another. When I met with judicial authorities from various countries in Europe, they were all very clear about the progress of China's judiciary. When the agreement expires in the future, it is expected to be brought up for negotiation to demand its return. I believe this kind of demand is very proper and reasonable. If our judiciary becomes increasingly sound, there will be no problem in recovering consular jurisdiction. (Special dispatch, 4th)

Second Sheet

International Commercial Telegram

丨Reuters Special Commercial Report, December 4th丨

Gold and Silver 93

▲London Gold Price: Today, 140 shillings and 6.5 pence, up 4.5 pence from yesterday.

▲London Silver: The London silver market was unchanged today. Spot price is 24.6875 pence, futures 24.8125 pence. Market conditions are stable, with India buying and China selling.

▲Mountly Silver: The Mountly silver market did not change much today.

▲Bombay Silver: The Bombay silver market was stable today. The spot price closed at 65 rupees and 6 annas, the same as yesterday's price.

Exchange Rates 94

▲GBP/USD: In the London foreign exchange market today, the authorities did not use the equalization fund. The GBP/USD exchange rate at 11:00 AM was $4.949375, down 8.125 from yesterday's closing rate. It fell another 125 in the morning to $4.948125, the most recent price.

▲GBP/FRF: The opening price was 75 francs and 9, down 12 pounds, with no changes in price at the time of transmission.

▲USD/GBP: In the New York foreign exchange market, the pound sterling remained weak. The opening USD/GBP exchange rate was $4.95, down 625, then fell another 25 to $4.9475.

Cotton and Wheat 95

▲US Cotton: The New York cotton market opened higher, rising by 23 points due to good demand and low pressure. Prices continued to rise in the morning, but market transactions were small and thin, due to fears that the upcoming Department of Agriculture report would show an increase in cotton production. Some quarters predict that this kind of apprehension will have a depressing effect on cotton prices.

▲US Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened in a stable fashion with little price change. Sentiment remained firm. According to the reports received, the supply of wheat next year will continue to decrease, the weather remains cold, and the demand for fodder is increasingly strong.

▲British Cotton: Liverpool cotton prices fell sharply today. At 1:00 PM, the January futures price was 6.66, down 7 points from yesterday's close.

▲British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was stable today. At 1:00 PM, the December futures price was unchanged at 4 shillings and 9.125 pence.

▲Indian Cotton: Bombay cotton futures rose slightly today due to buying by Japanese and brokers. Closing was stable. The price of Broach cotton for April-May delivery opened slightly volatile, but the close reached today's highest price, 222 rupees and 25, down 75 points.

Rubber 96

▲London: The rubber market was quiet today. At noon, the trading price for April-June delivery was 6.5625 pence, unchanged from yesterday's price.

▲New York: The New York rubber market opened higher than expected by several points. Market conditions remain active, and prices continue to trend upward.

Securities 97

▲New York: The factors favoring market conditions before the opening of the securities market were: (1) yesterday's slight drop in securities prices had stabilized its footing; (2) Washington government statisticians, based on public and private reports, predicted that this Christmas season would be excellent, the best since 1930. The unfavorable factors were the uncertainty of major commodity market conditions, which made general sentiment uneasy, and that the impetus for recent increases was lacking. At the same time, merchants had a wait-and-see attitude regarding developments in Washington. The stock market opened slightly active this morning, with prices fluctuating slightly, with both increases and decreases. Merchants' actions were very cautious. The market still seemed to show no signs of real change. The New York stock prices are listed below:
