Record of the Trial of Notorious Kidnapper Zheng Tangsheng's Conspiracy to Escape Prison 175

Passing Letters and Obtaining Pistols and Nitric Acid Through a Guard

Yesterday, the court interrogated the defendants separately, each attempting to shift the blame.

Zheng Tangsheng, a local notorious kidnapper involved in kidnapping for ransom, tearing up victims, and burying bodies in Shanghai and Tianjin, was apprehended by the French police in Tianjin around July of last year, brought to Shanghai, and prosecuted by the Second Special District Court. During the trial, the criminal once attempted suicide in the police station jail but was discovered, taken down, and sent to the hospital for treatment. He was then sentenced to death according to the Bandit Suppression Regulations. Zheng refused to accept the original verdict and appealed to the Jiangsu Provincial Government, which approved a retrial. However, Zheng, while detained in the heavy criminal section of the Second Special District Court's jail, recently plotted another escape. He wrote a letter, entrusting Liu Ruiting, a guard from Yangzhou, to deliver it to Li Jingen, a friend from Shanghai residing at No. 1, Lane 16, Renji Road, Pudong, asking him to obtain nitric acid and a pistol and arrange a time for the escape. However, the net of justice is inescapable. The plan was discovered by Jin Jiulin, the Chief Inspector of the French Concession's Special Agency, along with detectives Zhang Ziying and Qian Yumin. On the 16th of last month, Li Quangen was arrested at No. 25 Ailige Road and sent to the Second Special District Court for interrogation and detention. Simultaneously, Zheng and the guard Liu Ruiting were transferred from the jail to the procuratorate for investigation and prosecution. On the 24th of last month, Judge Qiu Huan-ying, together with Chief Prosecutor Chen Beisan, opened the court and tried the three defendants together. Li Quangen hired lawyer Shen Xingxia for his defense, and the hearing was adjourned to further review the facts, as detailed in previous reports. It is now known that Judge Qiu, who is presiding over the case, believes that the circumstances are serious and should be transferred to the local court for trial. Therefore, the case file was transferred to the president of the local court. At 10:00 AM yesterday, Wang Gangxu, the presiding judge of the criminal division, along with Chief Prosecutor Chen Beisan, opened a special court in the third courtroom upstairs. Lawyer Gu Shouxi appeared in court as the representative of the police. Lawyer Shen Xingxia, the defense attorney for the defendant Li Quangen, did not appear. After the court was declared open, the judge ordered the three defendants, Li, Liu, and Zheng, to be brought to the court to be questioned about their ages and hometowns.

Then, the police lawyer Gu Shouxi first explained the case and the articles of the criminal law under which Li Quangen was prosecuted, and submitted the letters and other items found on Li and in his home that Zheng had entrusted the guard Liu to deliver. Next, Prosecutor Chen stated the reasons for the prosecution, saying that the police lawyer had already detailed Zheng Tangsheng's intention to escape and Li Quangen's assistance in the escape plan. Regarding the guard Liu Ruiting's abuse of his position to transmit letters and collude for the prisoner, he is prosecuted under Article 175 of the criminal law. The court then ordered the defendants to be taken down for separate interrogation. First, Liu Ruiting was interrogated and testified that he had been a guard for two years, that he had delivered a letter for Zheng Tangsheng to Li Quangen, and had also mailed one for him. He had not spoken about anything else. As for whether guards can freely communicate with prisoners, he really didn't know. He had never discussed obtaining a gun with Zheng Tangsheng. He didn't know Zheng before. The written confession was given to him by another prisoner, A Si, who asked him to mail it on his behalf. He often went to the cell to deliver things. He didn't know Gao Lansheng, and there was no matter of worshipping the "old man". When asked whether Gao Lansheng's organization was a secret society or an assassination organization, Liu replied that he did not know. Then Li Quangen was brought to the court. He testified that he had known Zheng Tangsheng for a year, but they were not close friends. Zheng asked him to buy a pistol for suicide, not for escape. He didn't know the layout of the jail. Liu Ruiting came to his house once, but Zheng Tangsheng was not mentioned. Zheng Tangsheng testified that he had known Li Quangen for two years and Liu Ruiting for only three or four months. He asked Li to buy a pistol and nitric acid because he wanted to commit suicide, not escape. The layout of the jail was drawn by a prisoner who had been previously convicted. As for Liu Ruiting worshipping the "old man" Gao Lansheng, he heard it from others, and he didn't know about it. After the interrogation, the court reviewed the confessions and announced that the hearing would be adjourned to the afternoon of the eighth of this month for further interrogation. The defendants were returned to custody separately.

The Bank of China on the Bund to Rebuild a 28-Story Building 176

To Move to the Former Guohuo Bank Site Before the End of the Month

The Bank of China's General Administration and Shanghai Branch on Renji Road and the Bund have decided to relocate to the former Guohuo Bank site on Sanma Road and rebuild the Renji Road site into a 28-story building. The bank has completed the repairs to the former Guohuo Bank site and plans to complete the relocation before the end of this month, starting operations next year. As for the old site on Renji Road, it will be demolished and rebuilt. Once completed, it will be the only large building in China.

Efforts from All Parties Cooperating Give Excellent Impressions

Mr. Yi Meng, the General Manager of China-Hua Mei Tobacco Company, recently returned to Shanghai after inspecting domestic goods in Central and Northern China. Yesterday, he released a statement with the following remarks:
